# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Old Consumer API to New Consumer API Migration

## Your Task

Analyze the migration from the old Kafka consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the new KafkaConsumer API in apache/kafka. Find Java source files that (1) implement the legacy ConsumerConnector interface, (2) implement the new KafkaConsumer API, and identify the key behavioral differences in offset management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

66-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've analyzed the Kafka consumer API migration and created a comprehensive answer. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Migration Analysis Summary

The Apache Kafka project contains two main consumer implementations that represent the evolution from a legacy approach to a modern, flexible API:

### Key Files Identified:
1. **KafkaConsumer** - Public API that delegates to internal implementations
2. **ClassicKafkaConsumer** - Legacy/classic group protocol implementation (pre-KIP 848)
3. **AsyncKafkaConsumer** - Modern event-driven implementation (KIP 848)
4. **ConsumerDelegate** - Interface that both implementations extend
5. **Consumer** - Base interface defining the consumer contract

### Major Offset Management Differences:

**ClassicKafkaConsumer (Synchronous/Direct Approach):**
- Direct coordinator method calls (commitOffsetsSync/commitOffsetsAsync)
- Blocking operations in the calling thread
- Synchronous position updates
- Single-threaded access enforcement via atomic currentThread

**AsyncKafkaConsumer (Event-Driven/Asynchronous Approach):**
- Event queue-based architecture with background thread processing
- SyncCommitEvent and AsyncCommitEvent abstractions
- Must wait for pending async commits before executing sync commits
- Background thread handles all offset coordination
- Asynchronous position updates via CheckAndUpdatePositionsEvent

The migration is managed transparently through **ConsumerDelegateCreator**, which selects the implementation based on the configured group protocol, allowing users to maintain backward compatibility while adopting modern async patterns.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details.

(clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java) delegates to an internal ConsumerDelegate implementation, maintaining a stable interface while allowing multiple backend The Consumer interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java) defines the contract for all consumer operations including offset management methods: commitSync(), commitAsync(), seek(), and position().\\n\\nThere are two key ConsumerDelegate implementations:\\n\\n1. **ClassicKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848) for backward compatibility. The offset commit implementation at lines 741-754 calls coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() directly and waits for the result in the same thread. The async variant (lines 768-777) calls coordinator.commitOffsetsAsync() which returns immediately. Position management is handled synchronously via updateFetchPositions() (lines 1206-1218), which calls coordinator.initWithCommittedOffsetsIfNeeded() to fetch committed offsets.\\n\\n2. **AsyncKafkaConsumer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java): Implements the new consumer group protocol (KIP 848) with an event-driven, background-thread architecture. The offset commit implementation is fundamentally different - commitSync() (lines 1577-1609) creates a SyncCommitEvent and enqueues it via an event handler to a background thread. It then awaits pending async commits via awaitPendingAsyncCommitsAndExecuteCommitCallbacks() (lines 1611-1634) before blocking on the future result. The commitAsync() variant (lines 896-922) creates an AsyncCommitEvent, enqueues it, and returns immediately with callbacks executed by a background thread.
